Why do Americans insist on calling ham, Canadian bacon? Seriously the only country that produces "Canadian bacon" is America. In Canada, there is peameal ham, ham and bacon.   Peameal ham is ham with a cornmeal crust. This was invented in Canada.   Ham is regular ham.   Bacon is the strip bacon.  The thing Americans call Canadian bacon is what the British call back bacon. It is a British product that Americans make, and for some insane reason, they call it Canadian bacon when they got it from their own British settlers.

Here's a fact:   The McDonald's ice cream machines are generally NEVER broken.  They're manufactured by a company called Taylor Company. Here's the rub:  Only Taylor maintenance employees are allowed  to clean these machines.  It's a process that takes 4 hours. They are disassembled and thoroughly cleaned every two weeks.  However, McDonald's claims the machines undergo a daily heat treatment cycle to kill off any bacteria. So, the machines aren't broken, they're just down because nobody has  sanitized them.

Former McD's manager for a franchise store; The folded eggs come in a plastic packet. If you want good eggs in the morning ask for round or scrambled. Also, don't order breakfast at night, it is not very fresh and gets slapped into the microwave, except the sausage which is cooked to order at night. As for the ice cream ours could only be serviced by one company, who refused to come out half the time. They also caused an ice cream machine and OJ machine to catch fire once. And soft serve can't be served if the machine hasn't frozen it enough, but as long as it's still in the correct temp range we're allowed to do sundaes. If the machine has been overworked, it stays in a heat cycle sort of thing so you have to give it like an hour sometimes to cool off. I've watched it blast ice cream mix all over a coworker and floor when it was overworked. Super gross.

Fried apple pies disappeared from every fast food joint that sold them waaaay before anyone ever even heard of Michelle Obama - probably in the late 80s or maybe even earlier (although I think they're still available in some places overseas). I'm not a huge fast food fan but those fried pies were so freaking good. Blistery, flaky, thin crust enveloping saucy sweet cinnamony tender diced apples - OMG. You had to be careful because they were always volcanically hot and molten inside. Fried apple pies re-surfaced at KFC briefly some years ago and  Taco Bell offered something similar in the form of a Caramel Apple Empanada, but I'm pretty sure they're both gone again. I haven't been in either fast food place in a long time so I don't know for sure.

Eugene, The difference between the eggs: The round egg is called a round egg, the flat one is came a folded egg. Neither is microwaved, they are both cooked on the flat top grill in different shaped molds. The folded egg is weird because it is a scrambled rectangle, then folded over twice to make the square. The cooked eggs are held in a timed warming cabinet until they are used to make sandwiches, if the timer runs out, anything left in the cabinet has to be tossed. Fresh cooked never microwaved.

Lol not me screaming about the egg differences at my screen.  The Egg on the Egg McMuffin is round egg, or just an egg cracked into a metal round disc on the grill.  The "scrambled egg" is folded egg, and is liquid egg poured into a square metal form on the grill, then folded over itself.  And the egg found in the breakfast burrito is scrambled eggs that come with the burrito mix.  My first job was McDonald's, and I still remember this stuff. ğŸ¤£

This comment may get overlooked, but for anyone here who knows what happens to the food after these episodes or if they mentioned it before do let me know! I am curious to know as well
I work in a McDonalds in the UK and hereâ€™s a few pointless facts!  - the meat in cheeseburgers, hamburgers and Big Macs is a 10th of a pound. In my store, we literally call it 10:1 meat. - the McFlurry spoons are shaped like that bc theyâ€™re supposed to be mixed by a machine - the spoon clips onto the machine, which spins the McFlurry for 8 seconds. A McFlurry is supposed to weigh around 175 grams. - in order to combat waste, weâ€™re supposed to use a measured amount of ingredients; for example, 8 grams of onions on a burger. This is not regularly done bc imagine having to weigh everything before you put it on a burger. - A Big Mac with no pickles is virtually useless, bc there are pickles in Big Mac sauce. - I cannot speak for all stores, but in my store, the milkshake machine is very rarely broken. It is often used as an excuse for the machine being out of the specific shake and sundae mix used to make the items, or a misunderstanding by employees when the machine runs too low and automatically enters heat treatment. In order to fight any possible bacteria, shake machines are put into heat treatment every night and are thoroughly brush cleaned at least once a week. Managers want the machine on as much as possible (for profits) and employees can get in too much trouble for lying about the machine being out of commission; if someone tells you employees lie about it, its not true or that employee could be strongly penalised for it.

As a former mcdonalds employee: The folded egg that comes on the mcgriddle and biscuit sandwiches is frozen and then thawed in restaurant. The mcmuffin round eggs are cracked fresh and cooked shortly before assembly of the sandwich.  Always substitute the round egg instead of folded. It makes them 10x better.

Lol so all you need for hot fudge sauce is chocolate and some sort of oil. Melt the chocolate and add a bit of oil (preferable vegetable oil but coconut works if you want more of a magic shell effect) and make sure to mix it well. Depending on how much oil you use will effect runniness.

I'm a McDonald's employee, and my franchise offers it's employees free food for our breaks, so I am very familiar with all of these.  I agree, the Spicy Crispy Chicken is hands down my favorite thing on the menu, even over the Classic, which totally threw me, because I was a huge fan of the Southern Style years ago when we still had that.  The sausage egg and cheese McGriddle is what I eat when I get my break waaaaay early in a long shift, like I still have 7+ hours left, because I know it'll carry me through the rest of the day.  The hash brown is great; even though I eat it almost every day, it's still hard to say no to a free one.  The Quarter Pounder (with no cheese, because American cheese is the devil) is my favorite when my break falls during lunch/dinner hours. And we have fresh never frozen beef now, cooked when you order! We finally learned something! Somehow that makes a huge difference.  I still can't argue with people over the quality of our fries, and still go after them, even after I've had to clean out months old fries from our waste bucket that STILL looked new.  Also, you're welcome for that round egg on the McMuffin. It always cracks me up (see what I did there?) when people are like, "Oh, I don't know about that round egg, Jess, I don't know why it's yellow in the middle or why it's round, I always get the folded egg instead," and I'm like, "Yeah. It's round because we cook it inside a ring. We cook it with butter, and we crack a fresh egg into a ring. That's the yolk."

"The machine is broken" - aka we can't be bothered explaining the reason in detail so we say broken because it's easiest for you to understand. Hello from a past McEmployee in Ireland. Over here the machine would "break" regularly after making a very small few items because the machine has to cool back down after being used. Usually it takes about 30 minutes to an hour to be ready again. I always found it funny that the franchise refuses to replace the machines with more modern versions with a smarter cooling system, i forget the reasoning our big boss gave for not replacing it but it was generally just "we are not allowed to upgrade them until HQ say to".  Also McFlurry "straws" are Not straws xD Do not put them in your mouth, they connect to the machines that mix the ice-cream and toppings which you don't wanna be putting into your mouth ^^;

Actually about the quarter pounder half pounder thing, (although I'm not sure if this is still the case) quarter pounder patties weren't actually a quarter of a pound, they were a third, but people back then were too dumb to know what a third was so they would just say quarter to avoid explaining it. This means that a double quarter pounder would actually be two thirds which isn't a half. Though it's still closer to that than a whole pound, people nowadays are smarter and know what a third is even if a two thirds pounder doesn't really roll off the tongue but a half pounder wouldn't be accurate either. And Eugene's theory of double sounding better than half is also very valid.

I have to correct you guys on the fudge. from working at a McDonalds in the recent past, the fudge is in a bag, then it gets poured into a container to be warmed. we keep it in the area that the food is slid down to be bagged, then once it's warmed up properly and liquid and easy to dip into, we dip the cones into it. if it isn't the right consistency then the ice cream will fall in and get hard because it's the hard shell chocolate. we use the same for the ice cream in the cup but because it gets too cold again it won't stay hard or soft. it becomes kind of chunky and gooey inbetween.

Its going to be a lengthy post here. â€¼ï¸ I worked for mcds for 7 years(quit in August of 2021), the list is pretty accurate when it comes to sales, mcgriddles should be higher tho. (above the fish filet) I know it was 20 items, but they should have added the breakfast bagel sandwiches(it has the steak meat) and should have made the hotcakes into the breakfast deluxe; its hotcakes with scrambled eggs, (different from the folded egg from the mcgriddle) biscuit, sausage and hashbrown. Finally, about the ice cream machine, that machine is so delicate. If it has too much shake mix it will lock down, if it has too little shake mix it will lock down, if you don't clean the machine properly it will lock down. If we start running out of shake mix and people keep asking for ice cream we have to stop selling ice cream for the machine to not lock down. If it locks down it will take days to unlock and you have to call maintenance to help you out. It was a nightmare.
Fudge is real chocolate. The way it's prepared determines whether or not it hardens in colder temperatures

So far I have only seen two items get ranked, but as a former Mc Donalds employee, I have to spill the secrets. We serve three kinds of eggs for breakfast. on the egg McMuffins we serve round egg which is out the shell eggs we crack ourselves. on the biscuits, we serve "folded egg" wish is a package of about 9 little egg patties that we warm-up. for the breakfast and long-forgotten bagels we used scrambled eggs which was a carton on egg mix that was poured into a mold on the stove and shaken to get the scrambled egg look.  edit: I agree with Keith the McGriddle is awesome. with the caveat that is the only food that ever made me puke while working there.
